<script>
  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_a77feace-23f4-4d88-bc5d-f7cae0f0d8b1'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };
    if (typeof AppleID !== "undefined") {
      initAppleId();
    } else {
      initializeSiwa();
    }

</script>

  <span id="freeText13912303537914113654" style="display:none">When you're being hunted, who can you trust?<br /><br />For the first time since she escaped from her school many months ago, Eve can sleep soundly. She's living in Califia, a haven for women, protected from the terrifying fate that awaits orphaned girls in The New America.<br /><br />But her safety came at a price: She was forced to abandon Caleb, the boy she loves, wounded and alone at the city gates. When Eve gets word that Caleb is in trouble, she sets out into the wild again to rescue him, only to be captured and brought to the City of Sand, the capital of The New America.<br /><br />Trapped inside the City walls, Eve uncovers a shocking secret about her past--and is forced to confront the harsh reality of her future. When she discovers Caleb is alive, Eve attempts to flee her prison so they can be together--but the consequences could be deadly. She must make a desperate choice to save the ones she loves . . . or risk losing Caleb forever.<br /><br />In this breathless sequel to "Eve," Anna Carey returns to her tale of romance, adventure, and sacrifice in a world that is both wonderfully strange and chillingly familiar.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer264277088" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7789915418719233423"><b>Actual rating: 2.5 stars</b><br/><br/><br/>This is a difficult review to write. Most of the things I want to talk about (good and bad) involve giving away huge spoilers.  <em>Once</em> has a pretty big plot twist early in the story - one that I'm almost ashamed to admit I didn't see coming - making it close to impossible for me to adequately express my thoughts. But I'm going to try really hard to give a nice little run down of the book without ruining it for you.<br/><br/><em>Once</em> picks up a few months after the events in <em>Eve</em> and our p</span>
  <span id="freeText7789915418719233423" style="display:none"><b>Actual rating: 2.5 stars</b><br /><br /><br />This is a difficult review to write. Most of the things I want to talk about (good and bad) involve giving away huge spoilers.  <em>Once</em> has a pretty big plot twist early in the story - one that I'm almost ashamed to admit I didn't see coming - making it close to impossible for me to adequately express my thoughts. But I'm going to try really hard to give a nice little run down of the book without ruining it for you.<br /><br /><em>Once</em> picks up a few months after the events in <em>Eve</em> and our protagonist finds herself miserable in Califi, missing both Caleb and Arden. In this installment Eve, despite her best efforts, ends up in the King's clutches in the Sand City. There she is reunited with Caleb and members of the trail, who is now a wanted man for murder of New American soldiers. However, this doesn't seem to deter Eve and Caleb from stealing moments away together. But little does she know that the King has other plans for her. Big plans.<br /><br />As always, I'd like to start with the good. I was really looking forward to reading <em>Once</em> due to the crafty little cliffhanger at the end of <em>Eve</em>. I hate that nagging feeling of needing to know how things end because it bothers me over and over until I know. Thankfully, I got to find out my burning question of why the King wanted Eve so badly within the first 20% of the novel. Yay for me, but boo for you since you'll be reading a review where I attempt to skate around all the plot twists and revelations this book seemed to be chock-full of.  One thing that I really liked about <em>Once</em> was the setting. The City of Sand is in essence a restored Las Vegas and I could definitely visualize the different locations. Carey succeeds at painting the mental image of the city and bringing it to life. I expected no less considering I did enjoy Carey's writing in <em>Eve</em>. I also felt myself warming up to Eve this time around too. That is partly due to her making a better attempt at helping the friends she left behind and showing more concern for others.<br /><br />Unfortunately, I didn't quite enjoy this one as much as I did <em>Eve</em>, but I think that is mainly because I connected with the minor characters, who for the most part, are absent in <em>Once</em>. (I missed the dugout boys!) Instead we are introduced to a few newbies including the King, Beatrice (Eve's maid), and members of the trail. But most of the novel focuses on Eve and her constant struggle to break free from the hold the King has on her. And while I did start to warm up with her, after a while I found her actions to be a little too reckless (as they were in <em>Eve</em>) and I started feeling genuinely frustrated with both her and Caleb. It almost seemed like their decisions were intentionally poor just to move the plot in the direction Carey wanted it. For example, when Eve sneaks out the palace to meet Caleb, she's very concerned that he may get caught, but Caleb shrugs all concerns off. I understand that some teenagers feel invincible, but this felt like he didn't have any common sense. That surprised me because he seemed like a smarter character in Eve. He was much more cautious, but here I found him throwing all caution he used to have to the wind. By the end, he was practically flaunting a sign around his neck that read, "HERE I AM!"<br /><br />Despite my bigger disappointments with this installment, I didn't hate it and did find myself enjoying the interesting relationship between Eve and the King. And c'mon, that ending! I felt like Carey and HarperCollins punk'd me when I went to turn the page and all I saw was: ACKNOWLEDGMENTS. Cruel, I tell you!<br /><br />I'd recommend this book to fans of the first book, <em>Eve</em>. But if you disliked <em>Eve</em>, chances are <em>Once</em> will have little to offer you.<br /><br /><em>ARC was provided by HarperCollins via Edelweiss. Thank you!</em><br /><br />*cough* <a href="http://cuddlebuggery.com/2012/04/arc-book-review-once-by-anna-carey-and-signed-giveaway" rel="nofollow noopener">Signed giveaway for <i>Eve</i></a> on the blog! <br /><br />More reviews and other fantastical things at <a href="http://cuddlebuggery.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Cuddlebuggery Book Blog</a>.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="7789915418719233423" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1193857336627981261">NOOOOO! I REFUSE TO BELIEVE IT! Once again, Carey has managed to rip out my heart and leave me tortured for the next few months.<br/><br/>This book was a bit different in that the first was about Eve and Caleb surviving in the wild, and this was about Eve trying to escape her situation inside the city. But I loved it almost as much.   <span id="freeText1193857336627981261" style="display:none">NOOOOO! I REFUSE TO BELIEVE IT! Once again, Carey has managed to rip out my heart and leave me tortured for the next few months.<br /><br />This book was a bit different in that the first was about Eve and Caleb surviving in the wild, and this was about Eve trying to escape her situation inside the city. But I loved it almost as much. I'm sure some will even say this book is better than the first.<br /><br />One of my favorite scenes in the first book was when Eve first met Caleb and she insisted she knew what he wanted from her. I chuckled when Eve first met the king and insists she is not going to have his child. What I wasn't prepared for was his response.<br /><br />This book had me flipping through the pages like crazy as the story unfolded and reveal that everything is not as it seems. I don't want to say too much because the summary is left vague, so I'll keep it that way.<br /><br />The story wasn't unpredictable, but it had enough action and enough twists to keep you wanting to read on. And I love Eve and Caleb, and it was bittersweet to see them reunite.<br /><br />I'm sadden the book came to an end, and I am anxiously waiting for the next book.</span>

<div id="review_313524751" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/313524751" />
    <a title="B" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5206717-b"><img alt="B" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/313524751?book_show_action=true">Apr 16, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="B" class="user" itemprop="url" name="B" href="/user/show/5206717-b">B</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=read-reviewed">read-reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=2012-favorites">2012-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=gimme-the-next-book">gimme-the-next-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=hand-me-some-tissues">hand-me-some-tissues</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=judge-a-book-by-the-cover">judge-a-book-by-the-cover</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=didn-t-see-that-coming">didn-t-see-that-coming</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=2012-reads">2012-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=exceeded-my-expectations">exceeded-my-expectations</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=i-totally-saw-that-coming">i-totally-saw-that-coming</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=netgalley-edelweiss-arc">netgalley-edelweiss-arc</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer313524751" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8554808077666537006">I’ll admit, I went into <i>Once</i> with some slight trepidation. I read <i>Eve</i> a few weeks ago and absolutely loved it, and was instantly captivated by the scarily familiar world it took place in, the characters and their struggles and the great emotional impact it had on me. With all of that praise for <i>Eve</i>, and more, I looked forward to <i>Once</i> immensely, having high hopes for it, but was also a bit worried, wondering if it could live up to its predecessor. <br/><br/>And now, the big question: did it live up to <i>Eve</i>?</span>
  <span id="freeText8554808077666537006" style="display:none">I’ll admit, I went into <i>Once</i> with some slight trepidation. I read <i>Eve</i> a few weeks ago and absolutely loved it, and was instantly captivated by the scarily familiar world it took place in, the characters and their struggles and the great emotional impact it had on me. With all of that praise for <i>Eve</i>, and more, I looked forward to <i>Once</i> immensely, having high hopes for it, but was also a bit worried, wondering if it could live up to its predecessor. <br /><br />And now, the big question: did it live up to <i>Eve</i>? The answer to that is mostly yes, but also a little bit of no (I know, let me explain). The world in <i>Once</i> is just as captivating and richly detailed as the world in <i>Eve</i>, maybe even more so, and the plot <s>when it decides to actually show up</s> is one that is superior in both concept and execution than <i>Eve</i>’s. <br /><br />But you see what I wrote in strikethroughs right there? Yes, while the plot may be superior to <i>Eve</i>’s, and well executed, it shows up sporadically, as if taking a break every now and then. It pops into the book in short little bursts, then steps aside to make room for character development (a thing I absolutely <i>love</i> about this series, though – character development, relationship development, all types of development, and Carey somehow manages to make that thoroughly interesting and never boring), then everything just blows up in your face in the last ten percent or so. <br /><br /> But the thing is, while I would like to have had the plot show up less sporadically and remain more constant, that’s really the only complaint I have concerning <i>Once</i>. While I definitely would have liked for this installment to have had as much as an emotional impact on me as <i>Eve</i> did, those were pretty large shoes to fill and I didn’t really expect for those shoes to be filled in the first place. Aside from that, though, the character growth and relationship building throughout the novel is almost mesmerizing, and I only wish I had Carey’s skill in that department. As well as that, Carey manages to give us all as readers a fresh new cast of characters (thanks to a pretty huge twist in the beginning which makes way for an awesome, awesome plot) while making us care for each of them as we had for the cast of characters in <i>Eve</i>. <br /><br />Towards the end, <i>Once</i> is chock full of twists, turns and revelation that I was practically hyperventilating. Ending with a final, major twist and an equally as major cliffhanger, <i>Rise</i> has jumped into highly anticipated reads of 2013 list (and probably in my top five, as well), and I absolutely can’t wait to read it. And with what <i>Rise</i> is going to be about, I think it’s safe to say that the <i>Eve</i> trilogy may just end up being one of my favorite trilogies in young adult so far. </span>
  <a data-text-id="8554808077666537006" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_362007318" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/362007318" />
    <a title="Wendy Godding" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9286128-wendy-godding"><img alt="Wendy Godding" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/362007318?book_show_action=true">Jul 05, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Wendy Godding" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Wendy Godding" href="/user/show/9286128-wendy-godding">Wendy Godding</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of Eve</span></div>

        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer362007318" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12608110850150819970">After reading the other reviews on here I agree with most that is hard to write a proper review without giving away too much of the plot and the huge twist which - like everyone else it seems - I didn't see coming and is a great addition to the plot.<br/><br/>First the good. The premise is excellent. The writing is good too, Carey has a talent for getting the reader to read on, to always want more. <br/><br/>Now, the negatives. Eve is the most selfish character fathomable. I didn't actually find her that selfish in</span>
  <span id="freeText12608110850150819970" style="display:none">After reading the other reviews on here I agree with most that is hard to write a proper review without giving away too much of the plot and the huge twist which - like everyone else it seems - I didn't see coming and is a great addition to the plot.<br /><br />First the good. The premise is excellent. The writing is good too, Carey has a talent for getting the reader to read on, to always want more. <br /><br />Now, the negatives. Eve is the most selfish character fathomable. I didn't actually find her that selfish in the first book, even though she had been reviewed as such, but in this book she really is selfish. She spends an awful lot of time in a 'woe is me' head space with barely a thought to her friends left at the school or the danger Caleb is in. And again she makes poor decisions that are so obvious, trusts everyone that opens their mouths to her and seems to take risks with everyone's lives without ever really seeming to take that guilt on or even acknowledge the consequences of her choices. I didn't feel sorry for Eve at any point which was a shame as she did make a sacrifice, but if she hadn't harped on about it so much I might have felt it.<br /><br />And Caleb.... he seems to have been dumbed down for this book, making some questionable decisions.<br /><br />The plot and world building was also questionable. Set only thirty years in the future they talk about a world where there were once buildings a hundred stories high. What happened to them? How did a plague get rid of skyscrapers? I didn't get it. The plague is only fifteen years old, surely there are still people alive who remember the world 'before'. Maybe Carey needed to set it further in the future, or have something else change the world as I didn't understand how a plague brought down buildings.<br /><br />In all, it was an enjoyable read and I will look out for the next book in the trilogy simply because Carey has left us with another cliff hanger. If you loved Eve you will enjoy this, if you didn't love Eve, I'd say give it a miss.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12608110850150819970" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_388946072" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/388946072" />
    <a title="Donna {Book Passion For Life}" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3024878-donna-book-passion-for-life"><img alt="Donna {Book Passion For Life}" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1563622982p2/3024878.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/388946072?book_show_action=true">Aug 11, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Donna {Book Passion For Life}" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Donna {Book Passion For Life}" href="/user/show/3024878-donna-book-passion-for-life">Donna {Book Passion For Life}</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780062048561" href="/book/show/13622741-once">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3024878-donna-book-passion-for-life?shelf=ya-dystopian-scifi-thriller">ya-dystopian-scifi-thriller</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer388946072" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11168110230545184112"><b>**Spoilers if you haven't read Eve**</b><br/><br/>As soon as I finished Eve late Saturday night, I picked <i>Once</i> up straight away because after that ending, I had to know what was going to happen I'm so pleased to say, <i>Once</i> is a fantastic sequel - if not even better than Eve and once again, Anna Carey leaves me completely breathless with that killer ending.<br/><br/>After the shocking events in Eve, Eve is now safe in the lands of Califia. Unfortunately Caleb wasn't granted access because he is a male but even though he'</span>
  <span id="freeText11168110230545184112" style="display:none"><b>**Spoilers if you haven't read Eve**</b><br /><br />As soon as I finished Eve late Saturday night, I picked <i>Once</i> up straight away because after that ending, I had to know what was going to happen I'm so pleased to say, <i>Once</i> is a fantastic sequel - if not even better than Eve and once again, Anna Carey leaves me completely breathless with that killer ending.<br /><br />After the shocking events in Eve, Eve is now safe in the lands of Califia. Unfortunately Caleb wasn't granted access because he is a male but even though he's gone, Eve can't stop thinking of him. She loves him and she would do anything to see him again. When she hears about a stray being hurt in the wild, she knows it's Caleb and sets out to rescue him. However, once she arrives, she finds out it's a trap and she's soon on her way to meet the King. Once their Eve uncovers a shocking secret - one that changes her future forever but with Caleb still not far from her mind and the opportunity arises to see him again, she takes it...putting her at risk once again.<br /><br />What a great sequel! I always get nervous with sequel's because I've read so many lately that honestly, have been such a let down but not <i>Once. Once</i> is a heart-wrenching, jaw-dropping book, full of touching and heart-warming scenes. I didn't think it would be possible to love Eve and Caleb any more but in this book, you can't help love them more. The trials they are put through are hard and emotional and by the end of the book, I was a mess. I cried and literally screamed by the end of the book. Prepare to have tissue's with you. <br /><br />Anna Carey has done a fantastic job taking this series to a place I never thought she would. It's shocking, thrilling, captivating and I've already told you how emotional it is, but it's a series you must read! If you love Dystopia novel's then pick this series up now! </span>
  <a data-text-id="11168110230545184112" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer7517333645563278521">Book cover :<br/><br/>For the first time since she escaped from her school many months ago, Eve can sleep soundly. She's living in Califia, a haven for women, protected from the terrifying fate that awaits orphaned girls in The New America.<br/><br/>But her safety came at a price: She was forced to abandon Caleb, the boy she loves, wounded and alone at the city gates.   <span id="freeText7517333645563278521" style="display:none">Book cover :<br /><br />For the first time since she escaped from her school many months ago, Eve can sleep soundly. She's living in Califia, a haven for women, protected from the terrifying fate that awaits orphaned girls in The New America.<br /><br />But her safety came at a price: She was forced to abandon Caleb, the boy she loves, wounded and alone at the city gates. When Eve gets word that Caleb is in trouble, she sets out into the wild again to rescue him, only to be captured and brought to the City of Sand, the capital of The New America.<br /><br />Trapped inside the City walls, Eve uncovers a shocking secret about her past--and is forced to confront the harsh reality of her future. When she discovers Caleb is alive, Eve attempts to flee her prison so they can be together--but the consequences could be deadly. She must make a desperate choice to save the ones she loves . . . or risk losing Caleb forever.<br /><br />My comments: *** Spoilers ***<br /><br />So after Arden comes to Califia, she &amp; Arden decide to escape, after hearing some news that Caleb is out in the Wilds, in danger; hurt &amp; alone. They fall into a trap. Sgt Stark captures Eve &amp; Arden, taking Eve to the city of sand, &amp; Arden back to School to go and make babies. ARGH!<br /><br />Eve discovers that the King doesn't want her to re-populate, but that he is infact her father! Shock Horror! Eve is a Princess - how lovely for our main character.<br /><br />Eve misses Caleb, there is a price on his head. He is wanted dead for the murder of to American soldiers that he did not commit. Eve killed them, but they can hardly hold the Princess responsible...<br /><br />Caleb is working in the City of Sand. Working on an uprising, a revolt, with Moss (the leader of secret communications!) and some other people. He is creating a network of tunnels under the old flood sewers which will get people in to start a way, and help others escape. <br /><br />Caleb &amp; Eve have secret meetings, and one night, they have sex and fall asleep, awaking the next day far too late. They try to rush back to the palace and get Eve back there safe, but it doesnt work. Caleb is captured, taken to prison &amp; tortured. The King says he will release Caleb if she marries some loser that works for him. She agrees. But she doesnt want to. She loves Caleb. <br /><br />Before the wedding she manages to fit in time to visit her old school (she gives Arden a key to escape and hopes she can take Pip &amp; Ruby with her); and she has a plan to escape on the morning of her wedding. A few select people will help her. She escapes the palace, gets to the rendevous point at the tunnles to meet Caleb &amp; his crew... but something is wrong, no one is there. Except Sgt Stark &amp; his army of soldiers. Its a trap. They capture Eve, and as soon as Caleb &amp; his crew walk in... shots are fired. <br /><br />Eve is taken back to the Palace; it was her maid Beautrice that betrayed her for fear of her own daughters life. Eve is upset, but on one level understands. The King forces her to carry on as normal. She walks down the isle, the King lifts her veil. The wedding begins...<br />THE END<br /><br />Is Caleb dead? I doubt it very much<br /><br />Can't wait for the next installment!</span>

<div id="review_462771868" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/462771868" />
    <a title="YA Novelties" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11876185-ya-novelties"><img alt="YA Novelties" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1350268448p2/11876185.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/462771868?book_show_action=true">Nov 24, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="YA Novelties" class="user" itemprop="url" name="YA Novelties" href="/user/show/11876185-ya-novelties">YA Novelties</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer462771868" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16024916480290054318">Check this review out at <a href='http://yanovelties.blogspot.com/2012/11/review-once-by-anna-carey.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>our blog</a>!<br/><br/>1.5 Stars<br/><br/>After reading Eve, I was at a sort of a loss. Eve ended with such a perfect ending to keep the reader dying for Once, I remember reading an excerpt of this book and thinking "Meh...." There was nothing truly spectacular about Eve. After all, many of its themes and plot devices were ones already used in dystopians for years, and all of the characters bugged me. So now I really wonder why I read Once because honestly, it was worse than I expected.<br/><br/>Once beg</span>
  <span id="freeText16024916480290054318" style="display:none">Check this review out at <a href="http://yanovelties.blogspot.com/2012/11/review-once-by-anna-carey.html" rel="nofollow noopener">our blog</a>!<br /><br />1.5 Stars<br /><br />After reading Eve, I was at a sort of a loss. Eve ended with such a perfect ending to keep the reader dying for Once, I remember reading an excerpt of this book and thinking "Meh...." There was nothing truly spectacular about Eve. After all, many of its themes and plot devices were ones already used in dystopians for years, and all of the characters bugged me. So now I really wonder why I read Once because honestly, it was worse than I expected.<br /><br />Once begins a few months after the epic cliffhanger we were left off on. Eve is kind of off on her own in the women's haven, Califia, and suddenly, she discovers that the women there are willing to betray her for the safety of the rest of the women. OMG! Big shocker, isn't it? I mean, sacrificing one girl is an awfully cheap price for the safety of at least 100 women, so anyone with common sense can understand. The girl's new, doesn't really contribute much to Califia society, but Eve treats this news like it's the end of the world. Like, 'WHO DOESN'T LOVE ME ENOUGH TO KEEP ME?' Everyone, Eve, everyone. Basically, I just hate the protagonist of this series with a burning passion, which kind of causes my hatred of the series. <br /><br />I know I'm being a little harsh (OK, extremely) harsh on Eve. For most characters, I'm willing by bypass the sudden case of selfishness. However, for Eve, this has been a ongoing issue from Day 0. By now, I've been hoping for some form of her maturing, to make her seem relatable. Unfortunately, this just never happens. Throughout Once as well, Eve is still the same bratty girl who ran away from school the previous year. Not thinking anything through and believing that she's faultless when she causes tragedy to strike others.<br /><br />Additionally, the plot of this book sort of fell flat as well. We find out the secret behind Eve's past, and it's not that shocking. Many plot devices overused and repeatedly used in YA are used in Once. While I was reading this book, I felt like the plot was flowing similarly to how Torn by Amanda Hocking did. (Kind of a spoiler). Although there genres were different, Torn and Once are similar in plot and building up momentum for a sort of deadpan climax. The plot is almost identical to Torn, yet I loved Torn way more than Once, surprisingly. The thing is, Wendy in the Trylle trilogy matures and becomes a competent ruler over her people. Good luck with Eve managing to lead anyone, let along to not lead them into a trap, which she does repeatedly. <br /><br />There was just something crucial missing in Once that didn't allow me to appreciate anything. The writing was decent, but just couldn't hook me to this book. Many times, I nearly gave up on reading this because I was so frustrated with Eve, as you probably have guessed. Now, I'm just really disappointed with this series and the author, and really just can't imagine myself trying to finish the series with Rise.<br /><br />Angie @<a href="http://www.yanovelties.blogspot.com" rel="nofollow noopener">YA Novelties</a><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="16024916480290054318" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_253602213" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/253602213" />
    <a title="Debbie " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5098369-debbie"><img alt="Debbie " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589209937p2/5098369.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/253602213?book_show_action=true">Dec 30, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Debbie " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Debbie " href="/user/show/5098369-debbie">Debbie </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5098369-debbie?shelf=edelweiss">edelweiss</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer253602213" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2969157350148210277">I love, love, love Once. And for all of you who have read Eve, you know what the three “loves” mean. Anna Carey is an awesome, awesome, AWESOME! writer and she has written an irresistible series with Eve. I couldn't believe Carey could leave me on a more heart-breaking, torturous cliffhanger than she did in Eve, but yes she did it again arrrrrr! Eve and Caleb are my kind of YA couple. Eve is a strong, take-charge heroine, and Caleb is my strong, fun loving hero. Eve and Caleb are steamy hot this</span>
  <span id="freeText2969157350148210277" style="display:none">I love, love, love Once. And for all of you who have read Eve, you know what the three “loves” mean. Anna Carey is an awesome, awesome, AWESOME! writer and she has written an irresistible series with Eve. I couldn't believe Carey could leave me on a more heart-breaking, torturous cliffhanger than she did in Eve, but yes she did it again arrrrrr! Eve and Caleb are my kind of YA couple. Eve is a strong, take-charge heroine, and Caleb is my strong, fun loving hero. Eve and Caleb are steamy hot this time around with their romance and I do feel like Eve is going to kick some royal King's butt along with a few New America guards in the third book Rise. I think the title says it all. Can I just please have the third book now?!!!<br /><br />Eve has been living in Califia at the women’s settlement that Caleb helped her reach, to escape the King and his guards. But Eve keeps having nightmares that Caleb is dying. When one of the girl's from the settlement tells her a rumor about a guy that has a bad infection from a leg wound and that's he’s across the bridge in an abandoned warehouse, Eve is sure it's Caleb. And there's no way Eve’s not going back across the bridge into the wild to save Caleb. What's waiting for Eve at the warehouse isn't Caleb, but the last person she thought she would ever see again. Eve is now a prisoner, and on her way back to the City of Sand to be the King's wife…or that's what she thought until she arrives at the King's palace and finds out marrying her was not his intentions. But when the King tells her who he is and who she will become, let's just say Eve never saw this one coming, and neither did I.<br /><br />When Eve arrives at the palace she's still trying to find Caleb, but what she finds is Charles and the king's plans for Eve which doesn't include Caleb. I was very glad that Eve and Caleb were able to share their feelings for each other before all hell breaks out. Eve and Caleb are beautiful together. Eve dreams of being with Caleb, but the King and Charles are definitely not going to let that happen. Eve fears her nightmares for Caleb are going to come true, along with her fears of what she will have to do to save him.<br /><br />Anna Carey did not disappoint me with this awesome sequel to Eve, I love it, and Eve and Caleb romance is getting more amazing with each novel. I only hate having to wait another year for Rise, but I will because it's well worth the wait! I highly recommend Once as a must read!<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="2969157350148210277" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_434841262" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/434841262" />
    <a title="Kristin  Aragon" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4737702-kristin-aragon"><img alt="Kristin  Aragon" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1369243345p2/4737702.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/434841262?book_show_action=true">Oct 15, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kristin  Aragon" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kristin  Aragon" href="/user/show/4737702-kristin-aragon">Kristin  Aragon</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer434841262" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17233189899140568072">The sequel to Eve proved to not just be a filler book like most sequels in a trilogy are. The same amount of action and events occurred during the course of the story as well. The twist in the story that you are represented with is a complete shocker. It was something that I honestly never expected. Luckily the sequel wasn’t as depressing as the first book. It had a more determined feel and you see Eve grow as a character, from a scared little girl to a woman who should not be underestimated.<br/><br/>It </span>
  <span id="freeText17233189899140568072" style="display:none">The sequel to Eve proved to not just be a filler book like most sequels in a trilogy are. The same amount of action and events occurred during the course of the story as well. The twist in the story that you are represented with is a complete shocker. It was something that I honestly never expected. Luckily the sequel wasn’t as depressing as the first book. It had a more determined feel and you see Eve grow as a character, from a scared little girl to a woman who should not be underestimated.<br /><br />It starts basically where we left off. Eve is still in Califia, adjusting to the refugees’ camp that is just for women. She works in a bookstore and is under the impression that she is safe and well cared for. That is until Arden finally shows up looking like a man. The women panic and start saying that if Arden could find them and Eve so easily, why shouldn’t the King’s army not be able to? Eve and Arden overhear them plotting to give Eve up to the army if the time ever comes so they end up running away again. Only this time they do get caught. Arden is sent back to the schools and Eve is taken to the King where she learns the shocking truth about why she is really there. And to me it was quite a shocking revelation. If I was drinking water I would’ve done a spit-take worthy of legends. Thank God I didn’t coz my book would’ve looked like something out of the Lost Library Of Alexandria, not in excellent condition.<br /><br />I really loved where the story ended up going and was surprised a few times, but some of the things were also a bit predictable, like arranged marriages, suspicion of certain people and so forth. Eve wasn’t as naive and infuriating as she was in the first book and I ended up really loving her. I ended up felling really sorry for her because most people who she meets ends up betraying her in some way or the other.<br /><br />Caleb and Eve do reunite’ thank the Lord, but way to few times for my liking. They do end up doing the horizontal mambo (as Kristin would say =P) but the effect is short lived and does end quite tragically in a sense.<br /><br />Anna Carey did what some authors lack in doing. She kept you captivated through the entire book, which is difficult to do in a sequel book. I enjoyed reading it and recommend it to everyone. Give it a try. It might surprise you.<br /><br />~A Kelly M Review</span>
  <a data-text-id="17233189899140568072" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer15855604880386765937">(Source: I own a copy of this book.)<br/>This is book 2 in the ‘Eve’ series, and picks up 3 months after the end of book 1 ‘Eve’.<br/>Eve has now been in Califia for 3 months, and has no idea what has happened to Caleb, or if he’s even alive. When she hears that he might still be alive, she sneaks out to try and find him only to be captured by soldiers and taken to the city.<br/>Why is the King so desperate to get Eve? What has happened to Caleb? And what will happen to Eve now?<br/><br/><br/>This was a good story, and I lik</span>
  <span id="freeText15855604880386765937" style="display:none">(Source: I own a copy of this book.)<br />This is book 2 in the ‘Eve’ series, and picks up 3 months after the end of book 1 ‘Eve’.<br />Eve has now been in Califia for 3 months, and has no idea what has happened to Caleb, or if he’s even alive. When she hears that he might still be alive, she sneaks out to try and find him only to be captured by soldiers and taken to the city.<br />Why is the King so desperate to get Eve? What has happened to Caleb? And what will happen to Eve now?<br /><br /><br />This was a good story, and I liked it more than I liked book 1.<br /><br />Eve was quite strong in this book, and really tried to help and make changes that would benefit those who were still suffering. I thought she handled the big secret thrown at her relatively well, and I liked that she didn’t give up, even when things were tough. She could have been better at knowing when people were lying to her though.<br /><br />The storyline in this was quite different to that in ‘Eve’, but I think I actually liked this book better. This book didn’t seem to have the same issues as the first, and the whole thing just flowed better. I also liked the slightly faster pace. I was also glad that this book wasn’t just about travelling as so many middle books are.<br />The romance in this one progressed from what we got in book 1, but there was nothing graphic. I still don’t really love Caleb, but the romance was okay.<br />The ending was also alright, although we were left with a cliff-hanger, although it wasn’t a really exciting cliff-hanger.<br />Overall; much better than the first book.<br />7.5 out of 10.<br /></span>

  <span id="freeText2737604297354793893" style="display:none">At this point, the first book is my favorite of the two. <span id="freeTextContainer14639732614961733619">** 3.5 stars ** <br/><br/>This was another fast paced super quick read. There was lots of action and the plot became more complex. However the characters still didn’t fully grab me and make me feel anything for their situation. <br/><br/>Eve did show some character growth and there was an improvement on her character from the first book. Caleb however was an idiot. <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[ He was reckless, had no common sense or any thoughts of safety. So it really wasn’t much of a surprise that he was shot and apparently k</span></span>
  <span id="freeText14639732614961733619" style="display:none">** 3.5 stars ** <br /><br />This was another fast paced super quick read. There was lots of action and the plot became more complex. However the characters still didn’t fully grab me and make me feel anything for their situation. <br /><br />Eve did show some character growth and there was an improvement on her character from the first book. Caleb however was an idiot. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ He was reckless, had no common sense or any thoughts of safety. So it really wasn’t much of a surprise that he was shot and apparently killed.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br /><br />That plot twist with the King and Eve was quite a shocker and I wasn’t expecting it to happen so early into the book! But from then on the plot got predictable and my interest zoned in and out. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ The King is not surprisingly an asshole who doesn’t care about anything other than increasing the population and forcing Eve into an unwanted marriage just to produce an heir.  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br /><br />If there’s one thing I hate it’s a cliffhanger and both books have ended on one! But what the author does well is cliffhangers and both times I’ve started the next book immediately after because I couldn’t stand not knowing what happens next. <br /><br />Overall this was a slight improvement from the first book. The plot still didn’t completely have my full attention for the entire book but it was still a decent read. <br /></span>

<div id="review_276650790" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/276650790" />
    <a title="Amanda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5501124-amanda"><img alt="Amanda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1581282691p2/5501124.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/276650790?book_show_action=true">Feb 12, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amanda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amanda" href="/user/show/5501124-amanda">Amanda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5501124-amanda?shelf=july-2012-release">july-2012-release</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5501124-amanda?shelf=for-review">for-review</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5501124-amanda?shelf=harper-collins">harper-collins</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5501124-amanda?shelf=dystopian">dystopian</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5501124-amanda?shelf=review-on-the-blog">review-on-the-blog</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5501124-amanda?shelf=ya-lit">ya-lit</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer276650790" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11292641007257465965">A joint review with my co-blogger, Meg:<br/><br/>Once by Anna Carey is the second book in the Eve trilogy. Set in 2032, eighteen year old Eve is living in Califia, a female-only haven. It’s been three months since she arrived and had to leave Caleb behind. She was taken in by Maeve, one of the leaders, and has been helping out and getting to know the other women, but everyday she worries about Caleb, wondering if he’s even still alive.<br/><br/>Meg was the one who recommended Eve to me last year and while I enjoyed</span>
  <span id="freeText11292641007257465965" style="display:none">A joint review with my co-blogger, Meg:<br /><br />Once by Anna Carey is the second book in the Eve trilogy. Set in 2032, eighteen year old Eve is living in Califia, a female-only haven. It’s been three months since she arrived and had to leave Caleb behind. She was taken in by Maeve, one of the leaders, and has been helping out and getting to know the other women, but everyday she worries about Caleb, wondering if he’s even still alive.<br /><br />Meg was the one who recommended Eve to me last year and while I enjoyed it, I didn’t love it but I was definitely keen to read Once and find out what happened next and was really surprised by how much I enjoyed the sequel. There’s not a lot we can say plot-wise, a lot happens in this book and there are so many twists and surprises, but we don’t want to spoil anything. We especially don't want to give away too much about the first book in case you haven't read it yet.<br /><br />Meg: I had read Eve as an advanced copy before it was initially published and I really liked it, but didn't LOVE it. I picked up Once with the hope that it would be a little better than Eve. And it was! I found the first half of the book to go a little bit slowly, but the second half flew by. In fact, I would start reading on my lunch break and be crushed when my time was up and had to leave my book behind. I'm a librarian, but I never get to read on the job. I tweeted to Mands on my lunch break the last few days because having a minor meltdown about the suspense of the story.<br /><br />Mands: I really loved your tweets, Meg, you got me excited about this book, all over again!<br />I liked Eve a lot more this time around, she’s not as naive as she was in the first book and she’s quite brave, too. Eve finds out more details about her family and she shares more memories of her childhood with her mother, before she died from the virus. I like Caleb as well and knew he’d be back, resourceful boy that he is. Their love for each other is so sweet and I was happy with the progression in their relationship.<br /><br />Meg: I'm with Mands about the changes Eve experienced. She has a lot more common sense and street smarts this time around. I also loved her tenacity. She keeps overcoming obstacles throughout the series, but especially in Once. At one point, it seems that everything she thought she knew about herself and her life is a lie. But, she lifts herself up and tries again. Caleb, of course, came back into this story. How could he not? He's a sweet boy with a very strong will to live and a huge heart. He cares so much about the people around him, especially Eve, that he gives up anything he needs to help them. He's the epitome of selfless love. Their relationship is strong and intense, but fraught with obstacles (aren't all relationships?).<br /><br />Mands: You’re so right about him being selfless, Meg, and I agree about the obstacles, I know readers will be able to relate to their struggles.<br /><br />I enjoyed the writing and find the world that Anna has created very easy to picture. I already had a clear image in my mind of Califia and was looking forward to the change of scenery once Eve reaches The City of Sand (formerly Las Vegas). And it was great to see the world expanded upon, we get to see where the babies born in the Schools end up, I'd been wondering if they would ever be discussed or appear.<br /><br />Meg: I was also glad for the change of scenery when Eve makes it to The City of Sand. The road there is dangerous and filled with some pretty intense (and sometimes sad) moments. Is it everything she thought it would be? Well, that's for you to find out! The glimpses we got to see of the School and the babies was interesting. There's some serious emotion and serious suspense in the second half of Once, and I'm really looking forward to reading the final instalment of the trilogy.<br /><br /><br />Mands: While I wouldn't call the ending a cliffhanger, the final scene is something that the book was leading up to so it’s not a surprise and I think it will be a good place to pick up from in the final book, Rise (due out April 2013!)<br /><br />Meg: I agree that the ending isn't a cliffhanger, per se, but there are some unanswered questions and unexplained elements that I'm definitely wanting to find out more about in the final book. The key given Eve by a teacher? The directions Eve receives from a so-called reporter? Aargh. You should just read it already!!<br /><br />Once is a fast-paced novel with plenty of twists to keep you intrigued. If you read Eve or love dystopian YA, definitely pick up a copy of Once!<br /><br />Mands: A very big thank you to Harper Collins for my review copy.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11292641007257465965" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_235288712" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/235288712" />
    <a title="Carina Olsen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5457171-carina-olsen"><img alt="Carina Olsen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1566083624p2/5457171.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/235288712?book_show_action=true">Nov 14, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Carina Olsen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Carina Olsen" href="/user/show/5457171-carina-olsen">Carina Olsen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer235288712" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14966250125678840204">I should start by saying that if you have not read the first book in this series, Eve, yet, then you should not read this review. Because it will contain spoilers to the first book, and you really should not know those things if you have not read it yet ;) Also, my review of Once has a few small spoilers, but those can also be found by reading the summary :)<br/><br/>I want to start by saying that I LOVE the cover of this book :) It is simply stunning. Love that it follows the cover of Eve. Also love that</span>
  <span id="freeText14966250125678840204" style="display:none">I should start by saying that if you have not read the first book in this series, Eve, yet, then you should not read this review. Because it will contain spoilers to the first book, and you really should not know those things if you have not read it yet ;) Also, my review of Once has a few small spoilers, but those can also be found by reading the summary :)<br /><br />I want to start by saying that I LOVE the cover of this book :) It is simply stunning. Love that it follows the cover of Eve. Also love that the cover has something to do with stuff happening in the book ;) Sort of.<br /><br />Once start at the same place Eve ended. Only three months later. I don't really like time jumps, but, three months isn't really that long :) We get introduced to many new characters from the beginning, and I liked a few of them. Some, I did not like at all. Eve has been living in Califia for three months; she's still missing Caleb so much, and hoping to see him soon. <br /><br />But she is trying to move forward, but without forgetting about him. Which I was really happy about. Then, suddenly, someone lost arrives at Califia. But it is not Caleb. I really did like the surprise person that arrived. Liked it a lot. Also liked the dog; although what happened later with that killed me. <br /><br />Eve and the new visitor overhear the women living at Califia discussing what they really have planned for Eve if the soldiers ever catch up with her. It is then Eve decides it is time to leave, if there is any way to. But then someone claims to have seen Caleb outside the city, and she and the 'visitor' rush to find him. <br /><br />What they doesn't know, however, is that they are being set up. By some (evil) boy that was in the first book. Eve is then separated from her friend, and taken to the King in the City of Sand. Once there, she finds out why she really has been searched for. And what is supposed to happen to her next.<br /><br />But she also finds Caleb there. He has been there for weeks, working undercover, sort of. But they are all looking for him, accusing him of killing some soldiers; that he did not do. Meaning if he is caught, he will be put in prison and most likely executed. <br /><br />But so far he has not been spotted by anyone. Except for Eve. And they start meeting in secret, which is really risky, but oh, I really really really loved those parts. I love the romance in this book. So good. Although there was a part in the middle I didn't get. Wasn't sure if something happened, or not. Wish it was more obvious ;)<br /><br />Won't say anymore about the plot now; because more things happen :D Many spoilery things. Many bad things, but also kind of good things. Anyway, this book is amazing. I really loved it, although I did have a few problems reading at times, but that is my own issues ;p Once is just as exciting as Eve was. Something is always happening. <br /><br />And I still really liked the characters. Well, I really like Eve and Caleb :) I also liked that we got to learn more about the school where Eve's friends had been locked up. Although we didn't get an end with that. And I'm hoping it will all work out in book three; hoping the "schools" will get shut down :)<br /><br />I did not like the ending of this book. At all. See, it starts out all hopeful, but then that hope dies. Something horrible happens, and something horrible is about to happen. The cliffhanger is HUGE. Really huge. And for book three I am hoping what happened didn't really happen, and what will happen doesn't happen :D <br /><br />Also really hoping the wait for book three won't be so long.. but, considering this book isn't out until July I don't think book three will be out before next summer. How I will survive the wait, I do not know. It will be torturous. <br /><br />Anyway, this book is a must get when it comes out :) A really great sequel to Eve. Even with the evil cliffhanger. Once is a must read :) Also wanting to thank the author, Anna, for writing such amazing books. &lt;3 I'm writing this review because I got an ARC copy of Once :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="14966250125678840204" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_337476055" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/337476055" />
    <a title="Amber at Fall Into Books" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/7247649-amber-at-fall-into-books"><img alt="Amber at Fall Into Books" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1405223234p2/7247649.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/337476055?book_show_action=true">May 27, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amber at Fall Into Books" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amber at Fall Into Books" href="/user/show/7247649-amber-at-fall-into-books">Amber at Fall Into Books</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer337476055" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9008499688655752367">When I pick up a sequel, I expect an improvement over the writing in the first book. That usually is not the case in YA literature, I've noticed. I feel like the author (and the characters) should have learned from the mistakes made in the previous novel. Again, that more often than not, is not the case. Once is one of the many books that falls into the "didn't learn squat" category. This novel picks up a few months after Eve ended. In my opinion, if you loved Eve, then you'll love Once. The boo</span>
  <span id="freeText9008499688655752367" style="display:none">When I pick up a sequel, I expect an improvement over the writing in the first book. That usually is not the case in YA literature, I've noticed. I feel like the author (and the characters) should have learned from the mistakes made in the previous novel. Again, that more often than not, is not the case. Once is one of the many books that falls into the "didn't learn squat" category. This novel picks up a few months after Eve ended. In my opinion, if you loved Eve, then you'll love Once. The books aren't that different as far as what is good versus what is bad. The world-building is still fantastic, and the post-apocalyptic, dystopian world, is extremely dystopian. Also, there was actually one surprise that I did not see coming. The rest of the plot twists were pretty easy to predict, but the one at the beginning actually shocked me. There is a lot going on, plot-wise, in Once, and apparently that leaves no room for character development. Also, the pacing was off, and the plot felt forced at times. Overall, I wasn't blown away by this sequel. <br /><br />Didn't mind the fact that Eve was selfish and gullible in the first book? Well, then, you'll like her just fine in this one. She has not grown one bit, and she doesn't grow over the course of this novel either. She still trusts everyone, even though anyone should know by now not to. Also, she still cares more about herself than anyone else. I figured she'd grow out of that in this book, and that's why I gave the series another chance. However, she did not. Therefore, even though Once ended with ANOTHER cliffhanger (I'll go into my irritation with the author's plot devices a bit later), I more than likely won't read the finale of this trilogy. It's hard for me to care what's happening when I want to bash the main character's face in. Additionally, Caleb apparently grew stupid since Eve. He throws caution to the wind in this novel, and I wanted to smack him. The King was about the only interesting character, and he, at least, did not make me want to resort to violence. <br /><br />The pacing of this book felt rushed. Not enough time was spent on any one thing for the reader to fully grasp and feel what was happening. Also, a lot of what the characters did made no sense, leading me to believe that Carey had written herself into a bit of a corner and had to use her characters as plot devices. Oh, and speaking of plot devices, Carey uses the biggest one of all... AGAIN... this book ALSO ends on a cliffhanger. I despise cliffhangers. There are ways of resolving some issues and leaving others open that do not anger me, but when nothing is answered at the end of the book, I feel like I wasted hours of my life that I'll never get back. I know, that's a bit dramatic considering it's just a book, but that's how I feel, nonetheless. <br /><br />Now, onto the good stuff. I like to put the good stuff at the end so that people remember it better. It makes sense in my mind. Anyway, as I stated, the world-building is fantastic. I could literally picture City of Sand. Every time Eve moved locations, I could see the location in my mind as if I were there. That is good writing, in my opinion. Also, the first plot twist is a doozy. It's rare that an author shocks me, but Carey managed to. So for that, I applaud her. <br /><br />Overall, this book was completely different than I expected in some ways, and exactly what I expected in others. As I said earlier in the review, if you loved Eve, then you'll adore Once because it's a bit better than the first installment. If you didn't like Eve, then I'd skip this one because it's similar enough that you won't like it either. If you haven't tried Eve yet, I recommend checking it out from your library. This world is a bit different than the other dystopian worlds out there, and people who love dystopian more than anything are likely to fall in love with the world Carey has created. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9008499688655752367" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_380506467" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/380506467" />
    <a title="i." class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11422082-i"><img alt="i." src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1343715788p2/11422082.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/380506467?book_show_action=true">Jul 30, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="i." class="user" itemprop="url" name="i." href="/user/show/11422082-i">i.</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer380506467" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2087886201594177898">This is the second book of the Eve trilogy .At the beginning of the book we find Eve living in Califia, a women only community. She had to leave Caleb wounded to save herself. Arden , her former school mate, soon joins her but not for long,since they are both cheated into believing that Caleb is near and they fall into a trap. Arden in sent back to school and Eve is taken to the City of Sand where she learns that .....<br/><br/>You will have to read the book to know what she learns but it is something she</span>
  <span id="freeText2087886201594177898" style="display:none">This is the second book of the Eve trilogy .At the beginning of the book we find Eve living in Califia, a women only community. She had to leave Caleb wounded to save herself. Arden , her former school mate, soon joins her but not for long,since they are both cheated into believing that Caleb is near and they fall into a trap. Arden in sent back to school and Eve is taken to the City of Sand where she learns that .....<br /><br />You will have to read the book to know what she learns but it is something she did not see coming at all. From that moment on, I think the book becomes a mixture of dystopia, soap opera and fairy tale.<br /><br />They live in a dystopian world, the information given to the citizens is controlled and manipulated,they are afraid of the outside world and The city of Sand is an idyllic but fake place.<br /><br />Some parts of the plot remind me of a soap opera: there is the married man cheating on his wife,secret children,unrequited love and rendezvous at midnight .<br /><br />Then , the fairy tale part: the king (even self-proclaimed ones are still kings), the princess and the palace.<br /><br />There is no fairy tale ending, though, the book ends with a cliffhanger .<br /><br />The idea of people , even after the collapse of the world, accepting a monarchy in America seems a bit far-fetched and some of the decisions the main characters made were rather foolish . However I found the book entertaining , and Eve grew on me gradually .I will probably read the third book.<br /><br />An entertaining read for a hot summer day.<br /><br /><a href="http://www.theleisurediaries.blogspot.com" rel="nofollow noopener">The Leisure Diaries</a><br /></span>

<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('gKW/nZZWdIYs6gPcOeqDqyc/88XLjN//CVP/C7e5tmYL8r063lyGSgWioSjvMm6MmahfkErhPbgmheI+0+9ISg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('AiQ2/f+vWLest0/3ueO+lYHKlTsdjvO4QXemvMHroriJczRat6Wqe4X/7QNvO1OyP105bpzjEf9uobuJpb1clA==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

It means privilege, eternal beauty, and being something other than a secretary. It also means the power to manipulate the very fabric of reality. But if controlling what people eat, where they live, and how many children they have is the price of having it all, Adelice isn’t interested.\n \nNot that her feelings matter, because she slipped and used her hidden talent for a moment. <div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer5977625082310842710">Anna Carey has been a gift wrapper, face painter, nanny, horrific cocktail waitress, sofa saleswoman and children's book editor. She graduated from New York University and has an MFA in fiction from Brooklyn College. She currently lives in Los Angeles, where she can be found writing, reading, and referencing 90s pop culture. </span>
